</span></div></div><div class="entry-header"><h1 class="jeg_post_title">Ancient submerged bridge in Mallorca reveals early human settlement nearly 6,000 years ago</h1><div class="jeg_meta_container"><div class="jeg_post_meta jeg_post_meta_1"><div class="meta_left"><div class="jeg_meta_author">
<span class="meta_text">by</span>
<a href="https://archaeologymag.com/author/author1/">Dario Radley</a></div><div class="jeg_meta_date">
<a href="https://archaeologymag.com/2024/09/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-reveals-early-human-settlement/">September 3, 2024</a></div></div><div class="meta_right"></div></div></div></div><div class="jeg_share_top_container"></div><div class="jeg_ad jeg_article jnews_content_top_ads "><div class='ads-wrapper  '></div></div><div class="entry-content with-share"><div class="jeg_share_button share-float jeg_sticky_share clearfix share-normal"><div class="jeg_share_float_container"><div class="jeg_sharelist">

<a href="https://www.pinterest.com/pin/create/bookmarklet/?pinFave=1&url=https%3A%2F%2Farchaeologymag.com%2F2024%2F09%2Fsubmerged-bridge-in-mallorca-reveals-early-human-settlement%2F&media=https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-1.jpg&description=Ancient%20submerged%20bridge%20in%20Mallorca%20reveals%20early%20human%20settlement%20nearly%206%2C000%20years%20ago" rel='nofollow'  class="jeg_btn-pinterest "><i class="fa fa-pinterest"></i></a><a href="https://chart.googleapis.com/chart?chs=400x400&cht=qr&choe=UTF-8&chl=https%3A%2F%2Farchaeologymag.com%2F2024%2F09%2Fsubmerged-bridge-in-mallorca-reveals-early-human-settlement%2F" rel='nofollow'  class="jeg_btn-wechat "><i class="fa fa-wechat"></i></a></div>
<a href="#" class="jeg_btn-toggle"><i class="fa fa-share"></i></a></div></div></div><div class="content-inner "><p>Recent findings from an ancient submerged limestone bridge inside Genovesa Cave on the Spanish island of Mallorca suggest that humans settled the western Mediterranean much earlier than previously believed. This discovery, detailed in a study published in the journal Communications Earth &amp; Environment, has pushed back the timeline for human habitation on Mallorca by approximately 1,600 years.</p><figure id="attachment_42619" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-42619" style="width: 1024px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-1.jpg"><img data-lazyloaded="1" src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB4bWxucz0iaHR0cDovL3d3dy53My5vcmcvMjAwMC9zdmciIHdpZHRoPSIxMDI0IiBoZWlnaHQ9Ijc2OCIgdmlld0JveD0iMCAwIDEwMjQgNzY4Ij48cmVjdCB3aWR0aD0iMTAwJSIgaGVpZ2h0PSIxMDAlIiBzdHlsZT0iZmlsbDojY2ZkNGRiO2ZpbGwtb3BhY2l0eTogMC4xOyIvPjwvc3ZnPg==" fetchpriority="high" decoding="async" class="size-full wp-image-42619" data-src="https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-1.jpg" alt="Ancient submerged bridge in Mallorca reveals early human settlement nearly 6,000 years ago" width="1024" height="768" data-srcset="https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-1.jpg 1024w, https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-1-300x225.jpg 300w, https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-1-768x576.jpg 768w, https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-1-150x113.jpg 150w, https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-1-750x563.jpg 750w" data-sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px"/></a><figcaption id="caption-attachment-42619" class="wp-caption-text">An underwater view of the 5,600-year-old submerged limestone bridge located inside a submerged cave. Credit: R. Landreth</figcaption></figure><p>The submerged limestone bridge, which is 25 feet long and composed of large limestone blocks, was first discovered during a scuba-diving expedition in 2000. Initial estimates, based on pottery fragments found in the cave, suggested that the bridge was constructed around 4,400 years ago. However, these estimates were later deemed inaccurate due to the poor preservation of radiocarbon-dated materials like bones and pottery found nearby.</p><p>&ldquo;Earlier findings were based on fragmented <a class="wpg-linkify wpg-tooltip" title="&lt;h3 class=&quot;wpg-tooltip-title&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;wpg-tooltip-term-title&quot;&gt;Artifact&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;wpg-tooltip-content&quot;&gt;An artifact or artefact (British English) refers to any portable object or material that has been created, modified, or used by humans. It is the basic &quot;unit&quot; of archaeological analysis. Artifacts can vary widely in terms of size, material, and purpose. They can include tools, pottery, jewelry, weapons, clothing, and more. These diverse forms may at times be mistaken for ecofacts and features, with all three often coexisting within archaeological sites. Archaeologists study artifacts to learn about the technological advancements,&lt;p class=&quot;wpg-read-more&quot;&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://archaeologymag.com/encyclopedia/artifact/&quot;&gt;Read More&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;" href="https://archaeologymag.com/encyclopedia/artifact/" target="_blank">artifacts</a> and bone remains, leading to inconsistencies and doubts about the actual timeline of human settlement,&rdquo; explained Bogdan Onac, a professor of geology at the University of South Florida and the study&rsquo;s lead author.</p><p>The research team, led by Onac, revisited the bridge in recent years with a new focus on understanding local sea-level changes. By studying a distinct &ldquo;bathtub ring&rdquo; of mineral deposits, also known as speleothems, along the upper portion of the bridge, researchers were able to reconstruct historical sea levels and determine a more accurate date for the bridge&rsquo;s construction. These mineral formations, along with the coloration of the bridge, indicated that it was built nearly 6,000 years ago, aligning with a period of stable sea levels between 5,964 and 5,359 years ago.</p><figure id="attachment_42620" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-42620" style="width: 761px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-2.jpg"><img data-lazyloaded="1" src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB4bWxucz0iaHR0cDovL3d3dy53My5vcmcvMjAwMC9zdmciIHdpZHRoPSI3NjEiIGhlaWdodD0iOTUwIiB2aWV3Qm94PSIwIDAgNzYxIDk1MCI+PHJlY3Qgd2lkdGg9IjEwMCUiIGhlaWdodD0iMTAwJSIgc3R5bGU9ImZpbGw6I2NmZDRkYjtmaWxsLW9wYWNpdHk6IDAuMTsiLz48L3N2Zz4=" decoding="async" class="size-full wp-image-42620" data-src="https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-2.jpg" alt="Ancient submerged bridge in Mallorca reveals early human settlement nearly 6,000 years ago" width="761" height="950" data-srcset="https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-2.jpg 761w, https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-2-240x300.jpg 240w, https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-2-150x187.jpg 150w, https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-2-750x936.jpg 750w" data-sizes="(max-width: 761px) 100vw, 761px"/></a><figcaption id="caption-attachment-42620" class="wp-caption-text">Photograph of the stone-paved path leading to the bridge (person height = 167 cm). Credit: Onac, B.P., Polyak, V.J., Mitrovica, J.X. et al., Commun Earth Environ 5, 457 (2024)</figcaption></figure><p>&ldquo;The presence of this submerged bridge and other artifacts indicates a sophisticated level of activity, implying that early settlers recognized the cave&rsquo;s water resources and strategically built infrastructure to navigate it,&rdquo; Onac told CNN. This new timeline suggests that humans were present on Mallorca much earlier than previously believed.</p><div class='jnews_inline_related_post_wrapper left'><div class='jnews_inline_related_post'><div  class="jeg_postblock_21 jeg_postblock jeg_module_hook jeg_pagination_nextprev jeg_col_2o3 jnews_module_42618_0_677482826d9f6   " data-unique="jnews_module_42618_0_677482826d9f6"><div class="jeg_block_heading jeg_block_heading_7 jeg_subcat_right"><h3 class="jeg_block_title"><span>Related<strong>Stories</strong></span></h3></div><div class="jeg_block_container"><div class="jeg_posts jeg_load_more_flag"><article class="jeg_post jeg_pl_sm format-standard"><div class="jeg_thumb">
<a href="https://archaeologymag.com/2024/12/6th-century-bce-shipwreck-discovered-off-sicily/"><div class="thumbnail-container  size-715 "><img data-lazyloaded="1" src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB4bWxucz0iaHR0cDovL3d3dy53My5vcmcvMjAwMC9zdmciIHdpZHRoPSIxMjAiIGhlaWdodD0iODYiIHZpZXdCb3g9IjAgMCAxMjAgODYiPjxyZWN0IHdpZHRoPSIxMDAlIiBoZWlnaHQ9IjEwMCUiIHN0eWxlPSJmaWxsOiNjZmQ0ZGI7ZmlsbC1vcGFjaXR5OiAwLjE7Ii8+PC9zdmc+" width="120" height="86" data-src="https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/6th-century-bce-shipwreck-457-120x86.jpg" class="attachment-jnews-120x86 size-jnews-120x86 wp-post-image" alt="6th century BCE shipwreck discovered off Sicily" data-srcset="https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/6th-century-bce-shipwreck-457-120x86.jpg 120w, https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/6th-century-bce-shipwreck-457-350x250.jpg 350w, https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/6th-century-bce-shipwreck-457-750x536.jpg 750w, https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/6th-century-bce-shipwreck-457-1140x815.jpg 1140w" data-sizes="(max-width: 120px) 100vw, 120px" /></div></a></div><div class="jeg_postblock_content"><h3 class="jeg_post_title">
<a href="https://archaeologymag.com/2024/12/6th-century-bce-shipwreck-discovered-off-sicily/">6th century BCE shipwreck discovered off Sicily</a></h3><div class="jeg_post_meta"><div class="jeg_meta_date"><a href="https://archaeologymag.com/2024/12/6th-century-bce-shipwreck-discovered-off-sicily/" ><i class="fa fa-clock-o"></i> December 11, 2024</a></div></div></div></article><article class="jeg_post jeg_pl_sm format-standard"><div class="jeg_thumb">

<a href="https://archaeologymag.com/2024/11/skeletal-remains-from-mary-rose-shipwreck/">Skeletal remains from Mary Rose shipwreck reveal insights on aging and handedness effects on collarbones</a></h3><div class="jeg_post_meta"><div class="jeg_meta_date"><a href="https://archaeologymag.com/2024/11/skeletal-remains-from-mary-rose-shipwreck/" ><i class="fa fa-clock-o"></i> November 1, 2024</a></div></div></div></article></div><div class='module-overlay'><div class='preloader_type preloader_dot'><div class="module-preloader jeg_preloader dot">

<a href="#" class="prev disabled" title="Previous"><i class="fa fa-angle-left"></i></a>
<a href="#" class="next " title="Next"><i class="fa fa-angle-right"></i></a></div></div> <script type="litespeed/javascript">var jnews_module_42618_0_677482826d9f6={"header_icon":"","first_title":"Related","second_title":"Stories","url":"","header_type":"heading_7","header_background":"","header_secondary_background":"","header_text_color":"","header_line_color":"","header_accent_color":"","header_filter_category":"","header_filter_author":"","header_filter_tag":"","header_filter_text":"All","sticky_post":!1,"post_type":"post","content_type":"all","sponsor":!1,"number_post":"2","post_offset":0,"unique_content":"disable","include_post":"","included_only":!1,"exclude_post":42618,"include_category":"","exclude_category":"","include_author":"","include_tag":"552,30","exclude_tag":"","glossary_cat":"","glossary_tag":"","sort_by":"latest","date_format":"default","date_format_custom":"Y\/m\/d","force_normal_image_load":"","pagination_mode":"nextprev","pagination_nextprev_showtext":"","pagination_number_post":"2","pagination_scroll_limit":0,"boxed":"","boxed_shadow":"","el_id":"","el_class":"","scheme":"","column_width":"auto","title_color":"","accent_color":"","alt_color":"","excerpt_color":"","css":"","paged":1,"column_class":"jeg_col_2o3","class":"jnews_block_21"}</script> </div></div></div><p>The bridge is a significant find because it suggests a higher level of planning and resource use among early settlers. Researchers believe that the bridge, made of limestone blocks, was constructed to provide a dry path across a lake within the cave, facilitating access to a dry chamber beyond. This area may have served various purposes, including as a refuge, a ritual site, or storage to protect food from the hot climate of Mallorca.</p><p>&ldquo;The time when the bridge was constructed also shows that people were utilizing this cave much earlier than previously thought, closing the gap between eastern and western Mediterranean settlements,&rdquo; Onac said.</p><figure id="attachment_42621" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-42621" style="width: 1280px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-3.jpg"><img data-lazyloaded="1" src="data:image/svg+xml;base64,PHN2ZyB4bWxucz0iaHR0cDovL3d3dy53My5vcmcvMjAwMC9zdmciIHdpZHRoPSIxMjgwIiBoZWlnaHQ9IjU2NyIgdmlld0JveD0iMCAwIDEyODAgNTY3Ij48cmVjdCB3aWR0aD0iMTAwJSIgaGVpZ2h0PSIxMDAlIiBzdHlsZT0iZmlsbDojY2ZkNGRiO2ZpbGwtb3BhY2l0eTogMC4xOyIvPjwvc3ZnPg==" decoding="async" class="size-full wp-image-42621" data-src="https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-3.jpg" alt="Ancient submerged bridge in Mallorca reveals early human settlement nearly 6,000 years ago" width="1280" height="567" data-srcset="https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-3.jpg 1280w, https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-3-300x133.jpg 300w, https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-3-1024x454.jpg 1024w, https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-3-768x340.jpg 768w, https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-3-150x66.jpg 150w, https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-3-750x332.jpg 750w, https://archaeologymag.com/wp-content/uploads/submerged-bridge-in-mallorca-3-1140x505.jpg 1140w" data-sizes="(max-width: 1280px) 100vw, 1280px"/></a><figcaption id="caption-attachment-42621" class="wp-caption-text">Proposed timing for bridge construction. Credit: Onac, B.P., Polyak, V.J., Mitrovica, J.X. et al., Commun Earth Environ 5, 457 (2024)</figcaption></figure><p>Mallorca, one of the largest islands in the Mediterranean, was one of the last in the region to be inhabited. This is in stark contrast to other Mediterranean islands like Cyprus and Crete, which were settled at least 9,000 years ago. The island&rsquo;s hot, dry climate, combined with thin soil that made farming difficult, likely contributed to the delayed human settlement.</p><p>&ldquo;Mallorca&rsquo;s challenging environment and limited resources might have deterred early human settlers,&rdquo; Onac said. &ldquo;In contrast, other islands had more favorable environmental conditions and abundant resources, making them more attractive.&rdquo;</p><p>The discovery of the bridge and the new timeline for human settlement opens the door for further exploration and study. Researchers aim to better understand the broader implications of early human activity on the island and the reasons behind the construction of structures like the bridge in Genovesa Cave.</p><div style="background-color: #eaecea; border-left: 5px solid #0088FF;"><div style="margin-left: 05px;"><div style="padding-bottom: 05px; padding-top: 05px;"><strong>More information:</strong> Onac, B.P., Polyak, V.J., Mitrovica, J.X. et al. (2024). Submerged bridge constructed at least 5600&thinsp;years ago indicates early human arrival in Mallorca, Spain. <em>Commun Earth Environ</em> 5, 457. <a href="https://doi.org/10.1038/s43247-024-01584-4">DOI:10.1038/s43247-024-01584-4</a></div></div></div><p></p><hr><div style="background-color: #f9f9f9; border-left: 5px solid #01325D;"><div style="margin-left: 05px;"><div style="padding-bottom: 05px; padding-top: 05px;"><div class="content-inner" dir="auto"><div class="text-content clearfix with-meta" dir="auto" style="text-align: left;"><em><strong>Stay updated with us! </strong>Follow us on <a href="https://news.google.com/publications/CAAqBwgKMOrsigswnNLpAg?ceid=US:en&amp;oc=3">Google News</a>, <a href="https://flipboard.com/@archaeologynews/">Flipboard</a>, <a href="https://www.facebook.com/archaeology.news1">Facebook</a>, <a href="https://www.instagram.com/archaeology.news">Instagram</a>, <a href="https://www.threads.net/@archaeology.news">Threads</a>, <a href="https://twitter.com/Archaeology_Mag">Twitter</a>, and <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/company/archaeologynews">Linkedin</a>, and join our <a href="https://whatsapp.com/channel/0029VajFeaPISTkDL71nHq0z">WhatsApp</a> and <a href="https://t.me/archaeologymag">Telegram</a> channels for the latest in archaeology, all directly on your favorite platforms!</em></div></div></div></div></div><div class="jeg_post_tags"></div></div></div><div class="jeg_share_bottom_container"><div class="jeg_share_button share-bottom clearfix"><div class="jeg_sharelist">
